###begin article-title 0
###xml 109 131 109 131 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Pseudomonas aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 109 131 <span type="species:ncbi:287">Pseudomonas aeruginosa</span>
Transcriptome profiling defines a novel regulon modulated by the LysR-type transcriptional regulator MexT in Pseudomonas aeruginosa
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
###xml 110 132 110 132 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Pseudomonas aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 430 443 430 443 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 465 470 465 470 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexEF</italic>
###xml 697 701 697 701 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexE</italic>
###xml 811 824 811 824 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 844 860 844 860 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Escherichia coli</italic>
###xml 1161 1172 1161 1172 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Pseudomonas</italic>
###xml 1312 1323 1312 1323 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexEF-oprN,</italic>
###xml 95 100 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 110 132 <span type="species:ncbi:287">Pseudomonas aeruginosa</span>
###xml 430 448 <span type="species:ncbi:208964">P. aeruginosa PAO1</span>
###xml 811 824 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 844 860 <span type="species:ncbi:562">Escherichia coli</span>
The LysR-family regulator MexT modulates the expression of the MexEF-OprN efflux system in the human pathogen Pseudomonas aeruginosa. Recently, we demonstrated that MexT regulates certain virulence phenotypes, including the type-three secretion system and early attachment independent of its role in regulating MexEF-OprN. In this study, transcriptome profiling was utilized to investigate the global nature of MexT regulation in P. aeruginosa PAO1 and an isogenic mexEF mutant. Twelve genes of unknown function were highly induced by overexpressing MexT independent of MexEF-OprN. A well-conserved DNA motif was identified in the upstream regulatory region of nine of these genes and upstream of mexE. Reporter fusion analysis demonstrated that the expression of the genes was significantly induced by MexT in P. aeruginosa and a heterogenous Escherichia coli strain and that the conserved sequence was required for this induction. The conserved DNA motif was further characterized as the MexT binding site by site-directed mutagenesis and electrophoretic mobility shift assays. Genes containing this conserved regulatory sequence were identified across other Pseudomonas species, and their expression was activated by MexT. Thus, a novel regulon directly modulated by MexT, that includes but is independent of mexEF-oprN, has been identified.
###end p 1
###begin title 2
INTRODUCTION
###end title 2
###begin p 3
###xml 0 22 0 22 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Pseudomonas aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 183 205 183 205 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Pseudomonas aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 367 368 367 368 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1">1</xref>
###xml 502 515 502 515 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 898 899 898 899 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B2">2</xref>
###xml 999 1000 999 1000 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B3">3</xref>
###xml 1222 1225 1222 1225 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B3 B4 B5">3&#8211;5</xref>
###xml 0 22 <span type="species:ncbi:287">Pseudomonas aeruginosa</span>
###xml 173 181 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">patients</span>
###xml 183 205 <span type="species:ncbi:287">Pseudomonas aeruginosa</span>
###xml 502 515 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
Pseudomonas aeruginosa is a leading cause of hospital-acquired infections and remains the most important pathogen associated with chronic lung infections in cystic fibrosis patients. Pseudomonas aeruginosa is well known for its intrinsic resistance to a wide range of antimicrobial agents and its ability to develop multidrug resistance following antibiotic therapy (1). Resistance-Nodulation-Division (RND) efflux systems are responsible for much of the intrinsic and acquired multidrug resistance in P. aeruginosa and genes encoding 12 RND efflux pumps have been identified in its genome. To date, seven-MexAB-OprM, MexCD-OprJ, MexEF-OprN, MexGHI-OpmD, MexJK, MexXY and CzrAB-OpmN-have been functionally characterized and their expression is tightly regulated. Although these efflux pumps can exclude various antimicrobials, most of them are not induced by these substrates in wild-type strains (2). Nevertheless, genes encoding for RND efflux pumps are highly conserved in many living organisms (3) and, recently, increasing attention has been focused on understanding the physiological roles of efflux pumps, that probably precede antibiotics and are relevant to the behaviour of bacteria in their natural ecosystems (3-5). It is now evident that efflux pumps are involved in diverse cellular activities including functions such as the detoxification of intracellular metabolites, bacterial virulence in both animal and plant hosts, cell homeostasis and intercellular signal trafficking. However, little is known about how the expression of these efflux pumps is modulated within innate genetic networks to support these versatile cellular functions in response to changing environments.
###end p 3
###begin p 4
###xml 151 164 151 164 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 166 167 166 167 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B2">2</xref>
###xml 188 198 188 198 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexEF-oprN</italic>
###xml 318 328 318 328 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexEF-oprN</italic>
###xml 356 369 356 369 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 371 372 371 372 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B6">6</xref>
###xml 499 503 499 503 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nfxC</italic>
###xml 718 719 715 716 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B7">7</xref>
###xml 720 721 717 718 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B8">8</xref>
###xml 761 765 758 762 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nfxC</italic>
###xml 837 841 834 838 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B9 B10 B11">9&#8211;11</xref>
###xml 884 888 881 885 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nfxC</italic>
###xml 944 948 941 945 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>
###xml 1019 1020 1016 1017 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B9">9</xref>
###xml 1079 1083 1076 1080 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>
###xml 1219 1223 1216 1220 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nfxC</italic>
###xml 1265 1269 1262 1266 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>
###xml 1336 1340 1333 1337 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nfxC</italic>
###xml 1502 1503 1499 1500 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B9">9</xref>
###xml 1548 1552 1545 1549 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexS</italic>
###xml 1584 1588 1581 1585 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nfxC</italic>
###xml 1604 1606 1601 1603 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B11">11</xref>
###xml 1609 1613 1606 1610 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexS</italic>
###xml 1798 1802 1795 1799 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nfxC</italic>
###xml 2075 2077 2072 2074 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B12">12</xref>
###xml 2119 2129 2116 2126 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexEF-oprN</italic>
###xml 2221 2234 2218 2231 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 151 164 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 356 369 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 2221 2234 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
MexEF-OprN is a unique RND pump that is modulated by a transcriptional activator, while other RND pumps are modulated by transcriptional repressors in P. aeruginosa (2). The expression of mexEF-oprN is activated by a LysR-type transcriptional regulator (LTTR) MexT, which is encoded by a gene located just upstream of mexEF-oprN in the same orientation in P. aeruginosa (6). The MexEF-OprN system is normally quiescent in wild-type cells under normal laboratory conditions, but is highly induced in nfxC-type phenotypic mutants. These mutants exhibit increased resistance to chloramphenicol, trimethoprim and fluoroquinolones as well as exhibiting susceptibility to certain beta-lactam and aminoglycoside antibiotics (7,8). The underlying mechanisms leading to nfxC-type mutants are not fully understood but appear to be multifactorial (9-11). For example, the frequency of isolating nfxC-type mutants has been associated with mutations in the mexT gene of the parent strain that render the protein active or inactive (9). Indeed, several mutations in the nucleotide sequence of mexT were identified in different laboratory PAO1 strains rendering the protein inactive and leading to a low frequency in the isolation of nfxC-type mutants. In other PAO1 strains, the mexT sequence encoded an active protein leading to a high frequency of nfxC-type mutants. In this class of PAO1 strain, the authors suggest that the expression or activity of MexT is suppressed under normal laboratory growth conditions (9). More recently, a deletion in the adjacent mexS gene was shown to result in an nfxC-type mutation (11). mexS encodes a probable oxidoreductase but its role in modulating MexT function is as yet unknown. Nevertheless, in all cases, it appears a functional MexT is crucial for the generation of nfxC-type mutants and this function is suppressed under normal growth conditions. Accordingly, and in support of the demand theory of gene regulation whereby the design of molecular control mechanisms is generally dependent on the demand for expression of the regulated genes (12), it is predicted that the expression of mexEF-oprN and indeed other possible targets of MexT may be in high demand in natural environments of P. aeruginosa.
###end p 4
###begin p 5
###xml 12 22 12 22 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexEF-oprN</italic>
###xml 67 71 67 71 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexS</italic>
###xml 99 102 99 102 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">qrh</italic>
###xml 107 120 107 120 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 122 123 122 123 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B6">6</xref>
###xml 126 130 126 130 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexS</italic>
###xml 154 158 154 158 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>
###xml 263 265 263 265 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B13">13</xref>
###xml 427 451 427 451 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Azorhizobium caulinodans</italic>
###xml 531 534 531 534 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nod</italic>
###xml 541 543 541 543 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B14">14</xref>
###xml 556 559 556 559 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nod</italic>
###xml 604 608 604 608 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexE</italic>
###xml 656 657 656 657 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B6">6</xref>
###xml 698 702 698 702 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexS</italic>
###xml 729 732 729 732 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nod</italic>
###xml 107 120 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 427 451 <span type="species:ncbi:7">Azorhizobium caulinodans</span>
Besides the mexEF-oprN operon, MexT can activate the expression of mexS, previously referred to as qrh, in P. aeruginosa (6). mexS is located adjacent to mexT and transcribed in the opposite direction, which is a typical arrangement of genes controlled by LTTRs (13). A palindromic DNA sequence has been identified in the promoter region of target genes, to which LTTRs are known to bind. This LTTR box was first identified in Azorhizobium caulinodans as an interrupted palindrome with the sequence ATC-N9-GAT, referred to as the 'nod-box' (14). Indeed, a nod-box-like sequence in the promoter region of mexE has been proposed as the binding site of MexT (6). Interestingly, the promoter region of mexS does not contain a clear 'nod-box'.
###end p 5
###begin p 6
###xml 70 75 70 75 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nfxC-</italic>
###xml 225 227 225 227 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B15">15</xref>
###xml 298 300 298 300 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B16">16</xref>
###xml 471 473 471 473 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B15">15</xref>
###xml 474 476 474 476 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B17">17</xref>
###xml 683 696 683 696 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 703 705 703 705 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B18">18</xref>
###xml 854 867 854 867 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 904 908 904 908 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>
###xml 938 948 938 948 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexEF-oprN</italic>
###xml 972 983 972 983 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Pseudomonas</italic>
###xml 1006 1017 1006 1017 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Pseudomonas</italic>
###xml 1053 1057 1053 1057 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>
###xml 1072 1076 1072 1076 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexE</italic>
###xml 1142 1151 1142 1151 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. putida</italic>
###xml 683 701 <span type="species:ncbi:208964">P. aeruginosa PAO1</span>
###xml 854 867 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 1142 1158 <span type="species:ncbi:160488">P. putida KT2440</span>
In addition to antibiotic resistance, overexpression of MexEF-OprN in nfxC-type mutants has been linked to reduced levels of homoserine lactone-dependent virulence traits, including pyocyanin, elastase, rhamnolipids and PQS (15) and to reduced expression of type-three secretion effector proteins (16). It was suggested that MexEF-OprN mediates these effects via efflux of cell-signalling intermediates, which ultimately commits the cell to a state of reduced virulence (15,17). Recently, we have observed that MexT downregulates several virulence determinants, such as TTSS gene expression, pyocyanin biosynthesis and early surface attachment, in a MexEF-OprN independent manner in P. aeruginosa PAO1 (18). We have suggested that MexT acts as a more global regulator than previously described and novel target genes may be directly activated by MexT in P. aeruginosa. This is supported by the fact that mexT is not tightly linked to the mexEF-oprN in the genomes of most Pseudomonas species, according to Pseudomonas Genome Database (). For instances, mexT (PP_2826) and mexE (PP_3425) are located in totally different loci in the genome of P. putida KT2440 strain.
###end p 6
###begin p 7
###xml 251 261 251 261 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexEF-oprN</italic>
###xml 265 276 265 276 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Pseudomonas</italic>
Elucidating the transcriptional regulatory network linked to MexT will provide a new angle to understand the physiological roles of the MexEF-OprN pump in a broader context. In this study, we demonstrate the existence of a novel regulon incorporating mexEF-oprN in Pseudomonas species. MexT activates the expression of this novel regulon by binding to a conserved DNA motif in their promoter regions.
###end p 7

###xml 80 96 <span type="species:ncbi:562">Escherichia coli</span>
###xml 101 119 <span type="species:ncbi:208964">P. aeruginosa PAO1</span>
###xml 170 184 <span type="species:ncbi:294">P. fluorescens</span>
###xml 195 211 <span type="species:ncbi:160488">P. putida KT2440</span>
###xml 371 378 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 493 511 <span type="species:ncbi:208964">P. aeruginosa PAO1</span>
###xml 1110 1117 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 2558 2574 <span type="species:ncbi:160488">P. putida KT2440</span>
###xml 2646 2662 <span type="species:ncbi:160488">P. putida KT2440</span>
The bacterial strains and plasmids used in this study are shown in Table 1. All Escherichia coli and P. aeruginosa PAO1 strains were routinely grown at 37degreesC, while P. fluorescens PfO-1 and P. putida KT2440 strains were grown at 30degreesC in Luria-Bertani (LB) broth with aeration. When required, antibiotics were added at the following concentrations (microg/ml): E. coli, ampicillin (Ap, 50), kanamycin (Km, 50), chloramphenicol (Cm, 20), tetracycline (Tc, 10) or gentamicin (Gm, 10); P. aeruginosa PAO1, carbenicillin (Cb, 200), gentamicin (Gm, 50), tetracycline (Tc, 50) or streptomycin (Str, 200). ###begin title 13
Molecular biology procedures
###end title 13
###begin p 14
###xml 106 108 106 108 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B19">19</xref>
All routine molecular biology procedures were carried out as described in the standard laboratory manual (19). All DNA primers used in this study are listed in .

###begin title 15
Expression profiling experiments
###end title 15
###begin p 16
###xml 30 34 30 34 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>
###xml 44 54 44 50 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;mexEF</italic>
###xml 64 68 60 64 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>
###xml 203 206 193 196 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">600</sub>
###xml 564 577 554 567 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 1275 1276 1263 1264 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 564 577 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
PAO1 (pME6032), PAO1 (pME6032-mexT) and PAO1DeltamexEF (pME6032-mexT) were grown at 37degreesC shaking (150 r.p.m.) in 20 ml of LB medium supplemented with tetracycline in 100-ml culture flasks. At an OD600 of 0.5, cell cultures were mixed with Qiagen RNAprotect Bacteria Reagent (Ratio of 1:2) to stabilize RNA. Total RNA was prepared with an RNeasy mini kit (Qiagen) and contaminating DNA was removed by RNase-free DNase I (Ambion). For each strain, RNA was prepared from three independent batch cultures. cDNA synthesis and hybridization to Affymetrix GeneChip P. aeruginosa genome arrays were carried out by a commercial Affymetrix Genechip service supplier (Conway Institute of Biomolecular & Biomedical Research, UCD, Ireland). Array data were normalized using the GC-RMA algorithm, and the data were then further analyzed using the microarray software package Genespring GX 10.0.1 (Agilent). To visualize the microarray data, MA plots (linear regression of log ratio, M, against average intensity, A) were generated by Genespring GX software, and 3D scatter plots on log2 based intensity data obtained from three samples were generated by SigmaPlot 11 software (Systat Software Inc.). Genes whose levels of expression were significantly influenced (Fold change >/= 2, P </= 0.05) were identified with Genespring GX, using a Benjamini-Hochberg multiple-testing correction and a false detection rate of 5%. The full list of genes whose expression was significantly altered is shown in .
###end p 16
###begin p 17
###xml 776 780 736 740 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">clpX</italic>
###xml 270 273 <span type="species:ncbi:11866?0.5863095238095238|species:ncbi:12321?0.21726190476190477">AMV</span>
To validate the microarray results, semi-quantitative reverse transcription PCR analysis was carried out using RNA samples prepared from biological replicates not used in the arrays. Two hundred nanograms of RNA samples were reverse transcribed using random primers and AMV reverse transcriptase (Promega). 1/100 aliquot of the reaction mixture was used as template in the subsequent PCR. PCR (20 microl reaction volume) was performed with the GoTaq(R) Green Master Mix (Promega) with the following conditions: 95degreesC for 3 min; 30 cycles of 30 s at 95degreesC; 30 s at 55degreesC and 30 s at 72degreesC; 10-min elongation at 72degreesC. For visualization, 10 microl of the resulting PCR was subjected to agarose gel electrophoresis and stained with ethidium bromide. The clpX gene was used as an internal control to ensure equal amounts of RNA were used in all samples.
###end p 17
###begin title 18
###xml 18 22 18 22 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nfxC</italic>
###xml 38 51 38 47 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nfxC&#916;mexT</italic>
Generation of PAO1nfxC mutant and PAO1nfxCDeltamexT strains
###end title 18
###begin p 19
###xml 4 8 4 8 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nfxC</italic>
###xml 159 163 155 159 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nfxC</italic>
###xml 178 179 174 175 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B7">7</xref>
###xml 186 190 182 186 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>
###xml 234 238 230 234 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nfxC</italic>
PAO1nfxC was selected by plating the wild-type strain PAO1 on LB agar plates containing chloramphenicol at 600 microg/ml, a condition that exclusively selects nfxC-type mutants (7). The mexT ORF and 500-bp upstream region of this PAO1nfxC strain had no sequence alteration(s) compared to the parental PAO1 strain.
###end p 19
###begin p 20
###xml 26 39 26 35 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nfxC&#916;mexT</italic>
###xml 103 107 99 103 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>
###xml 178 182 174 178 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>
###xml 364 367 360 363 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">FRT</italic>
###xml 425 427 421 423 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B20">20</xref>
###xml 499 503 495 499 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>
###xml 511 515 507 511 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nfxC</italic>
###xml 573 579 569 575 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 581 583 577 579 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B20">20</xref>
###xml 713 715 709 711 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B20">20</xref>
In order to construct PAO1nfxCDeltamexT, a 1-kb SacI-KpnI upstream region including the start codon of mexT, and a 1-kb KpnI-BamHI downstream region containing the stop codon of mexT, were PCR-amplified and linked together. The resulting 2-kb fragment was cloned into the suicide plasmid pEX18Tc digested with SacI and BamHI. A 1.1-kb KpnI fragment containing the FRT gentamicin-resistance (Gm) cassette from plasmid pPS856 (20) was then inserted in-between the flanking regions on the plasmid. The mexT of PAO1nfxC was then replaced with the plasmid as described by Hoang et al. (20). The Gm-resistance sequence in the chromosome was removed by introducing plasmid pFLP2, which carries the Flp recombinase gene (20). Correct insertion in the constructed mutant was verified by PCR using primers bind to flanking chromosomal regions of the fragments cloned in pEX18Tc.
###end p 20
###begin title 21
###xml 29 33 29 33 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lacZ</italic>
Construction of the promoter-lacZ reporter gene fusions and beta-galactosidase assays
###end title 21
###begin p 22
###xml 226 228 226 228 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B21">21</xref>
###xml 349 356 349 356 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T1">Table 1</xref>
###xml 403 416 403 416 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 451 458 451 458 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 488 492 488 492 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">hemA</italic>
###xml 526 533 521 528 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T1">Table 1</xref>
###xml 676 678 671 673 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B22">22</xref>
###xml 836 840 827 831 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>
###xml 849 853 840 844 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nfxC</italic>
###xml 912 916 903 907 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nfxC</italic>
###xml 948 961 939 952 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 1106 1113 1093 1100 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 1190 1192 1177 1179 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B19">19</xref>
###xml 403 416 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 451 458 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 948 961 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 1106 1113 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
The promoter region of each putative MexT target gene was PCR-amplified and TA-cloned into pCR2.1-TOPO (Invitrogen). The site-directed mutagenesis of the conserved DNA motif was performed by the protocol described previously (21). Once confirmed by sequencing, the promoter regions were subcloned into the broad-host low-copy-number plasmid pMP190 (Table 1). The resulting plasmids were introduced into P. aeruginosa strains by conjugal transfer from E. coli donor strain ST18. ST18 is a hemA mutant of S17-1lambdapir strain (Table 1), and can be easily selected against as its growth is strictly dependent on the presence of 5-aminolevulinic acid (5-ALA), even in LB medium (22). Therefore, 50 microg/ml of 5-ALA was added to the medium during conjugation and omitted when selecting for trans-conjugants. Since PAO1 containing pME6032-mexT and PAO1nfxC strains have a high chloramphenicol resistance due to the nfxC phenotype, all trans-conjugant P. aeruginosa cells containing pMP190-derived plasmids were selected on LB agar supplemented with 200 microg/ml streptomycin. The plasmid transformation into E. coli strains in this study was done by routine chemical competent cell protocol (19).
###end p 22
###begin p 23
###xml 282 285 273 276 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">600</sub>
###xml 365 367 353 355 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B23">23</xref>
For beta-galactosidase assays, cells were grown overnight in LB broth supplemented with appropriate antibiotics, then 1:50 diluted into 10 ml fresh medium in 100-ml culture flasks and incubated at 37degreesC shaking at 150 r.p.m. Cells were recovered at logarithmic growth phase (OD600 0.5-1.2), and beta-galactosidase assays were performed as described by Miller (23). Data are the mean of two independent experiments with triplicate samples.
###end p 23
###begin title 24
###xml 19 20 19 20 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sub>
Purification of His6-MexT
###end title 24
###begin p 25
###xml 51 52 51 52 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sub>
###xml 215 219 215 219 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>
###xml 308 312 308 312 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>
###xml 397 404 397 404 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T1">Table 1</xref>
###xml 446 453 446 453 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 840 842 818 820 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TM</sup>
###xml 1091 1093 1055 1057 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TM</sup>
###xml 1258 1260 1220 1222 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TM</sup>
###xml 446 453 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
The plasmids used to overexpress the C-terminal His6-tagged MexT proteins were constructed by PCR-amplifying the MexT coding sequence and cloned into NcoI-XhoI sites of pET28a. The plasmid harbouring the functional mexT from PAO1 was designated as pETmexTH6C, while the plasmid harbouring the non-functional mexT due to a mutation of the 39th amino acid Ala to Val was designated as pETmexTm1H6C (Table 1). The plasmids were transformed into the E. coli expression host strain BL21-CodonPlus(DE3)-RIPL (Merck) and grown at 37degreesC with vigorous shaking in 200 ml of LB medium containing kanamycin (50 microg/ml) to an OD600 of 1. The cells were then induced with 1 mM IPTG and allowed to express for 1 h at 37degreesC. The cells were harvested by centrifugation and stored overnight at -20degreesC. The pellet was resuspended in CelLyticTM B II buffer (Sigma(R)) (10 ml per gram cell paste) with 5 microg/ml DNase and 200 microl per gram cell paste of Protease Inhibitor Cocktail (Sigma(R)). The soluble proteins were extracted according to manufacturer's instructions (Sigma(R), CelLyticTM B II, Bacterial Cell Lysis Extraction Reagent). The protein extract were applied to a Poly-Prep(R) Chromatography Column (Bio-Rad) containing 1 volume of HIS-SelectTM Nickel Affinity Gel (Sigma(R)). The resin was previously washed with 2 vol of deionized sterile water and equilibrated with 2 vol of Wash buffer (HEPES 100 mM, pH 7.5, 1 mM Imidazole). After all the protein extract was loaded, the column was washed twice with 2 vol of Wash buffer. The His-tag proteins were eluted with 1 vol of Elution buffer (HEPES 100 mM, pH 7.5, 500 mM Imidazole) and their homogeneity was verified by sodium dodecyl sulphate polyacrylamide gel electrophoresis (SDS-PAGE). The protein was then either immediately frozen with 20% of glycerol at -80degreesC for later use or promptly used for the electrophoretic mobility shift assay (EMSA). The protein concentrations were determined by the Bio-Rad method.
###end p 25
###begin title 26
EMSAs
###end title 26
###begin p 27
DNA probes of 207 bp containing the putative binding region were generated by PCR using pMP-PA4881p (intact motif) or pMP-4881m1p (mutated motif) as templates using the primer pair fullmexTboxF and fullmexTboxR. The two purified PCR products were 3'-end-labelled with digoxigenin following the manufacturer instruction (Roche Applied Science). The EMSA was carried out using the DIG Gel Shift Kit 2nd Generation (Roche Applied Science) as recommended, with some modifications. Ten fmoles of the DIG-labelled fragment and a range of 0-300 ng of MexT protein were added to the binding reaction. The mixture was allowed to proceed for 45 min at room temperature. The samples were separated by electrophoresis on 6% native polyacrylamide gels and transferred to Hybond-N blotting membrane (Amersham Life Science) by electroblotting. Protein-DNA complexes were visualized by NBT/BCIP according to manufacturer's instructions (Roche Applied Science). Competition experiments were performed with 200 pmol of unlabelled double-stranded oligonucleotide. The labelled and non-labelled probes were mixed to the binding buffer before adding the protein for the binding reaction.
###end p 27
###begin title 28
Identification of a conserved regulatory sequence
###end title 28
###begin p 29
###xml 330 332 330 332 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
For the identification of a conserved regulatory sequence motif in the upstream region of co-regulated genes, the 500-bp sequence upstream of the translational start site of each gene induced by MexT was obtained from the '' database. Sequence motifs common to the upstream regions were identified by the online MEME software () (24) with a motif width range of 5-20 bp and the occurrences of a single motif distributed among the sequences between zero or one per sequence.
###end p 29
###begin title 30
RESULTS
###end title 30
###begin title 31
###xml 27 40 27 40 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 27 40 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
Transcriptome profiling of P. aeruginosa strains overexpressing MexT
###end title 31
###begin p 32
###xml 248 253 248 253 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexEF</italic>
###xml 437 441 437 441 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>
###xml 501 505 501 505 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>
###xml 537 550 537 550 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 692 695 688 691 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tac</italic>
###xml 717 719 713 715 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B18">18</xref>
###xml 733 746 729 742 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 864 868 860 864 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>
###xml 921 926 917 922 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexEF</italic>
###xml 955 966 951 958 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;mexEF,</italic>
###xml 986 990 978 982 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>
###xml 537 555 <span type="species:ncbi:208964">P. aeruginosa PAO1</span>
###xml 733 746 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
In order to assess the global regulatory nature of the LysR-family transcriptional regulator MexT, independent of its induction of the MexEF-OprN efflux system, whole-genome transcriptome profiling was carried out on PAO1 wild-type and an isogenic mexEF mutant overexpressing MexT. In the PAO1 strain used in this study MexT is quiescent under normal laboratory growth conditions. However, when the entire ORF and 600-bp upstream of the mexT gene were cloned on plasmid pME6032 (designated as pME6032-mexT), MexT was fully functional in P. aeruginosa PAO1, increasing the minimum inhibitory concentration (MIC) of chloramphenicol from 32 to 2048 microg/ml, even without IPTG induction of the tac promoter on pME6032 (18). Affymetrix P. aeruginosa whole-genome microarrays were used to compare the transcription profiles of PAO1 wild-type containing either pME6032-mexT or the empty vector control pME6032 and an isogenic mexEF deletion mutant strain, PAO1DeltamexEF, containing pME6032-mexT, during Mid-logarithmic growth conditions. Thus, we identified a potential MexT regulon and differentiated those targets that were dependent or independent of the MexEF-OprN efflux pump.
###end p 32
###begin p 33
###xml 172 180 172 180 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 198 202 198 202 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>
###xml 231 233 231 233 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">++</sup>
###xml 227 233 227 233 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT<sup>++</sup></italic>
###xml 378 379 376 377 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 465 472 459 466 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T2">Table 2</xref>
###xml 661 669 655 663 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 804 806 794 796 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">++</sup>
###xml 789 806 783 796 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;mexEF mexT<sup>++</sup></italic>
###xml 834 835 824 825 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 835 836 825 826 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 830 836 820 826 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT<sup>+</sup><sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 934 936 920 922 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">++</sup>
###xml 919 936 909 922 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;mexEF mexT<sup>++</sup></italic>
###xml 983 988 969 974 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexEF</italic>
###xml 1051 1061 1037 1047 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexEF-oprN</italic>
###xml 1133 1135 1115 1117 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">++</sup>
###xml 1118 1135 1104 1117 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;mexEF mexT<sup>++</sup></italic>
###xml 1157 1159 1139 1141 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">++</sup>
###xml 1153 1159 1135 1141 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT<sup>++</sup></italic>
###xml 1161 1168 1143 1150 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T2">Table 2</xref>
###xml 1225 1230 1207 1212 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexEF</italic>
###xml 1305 1307 1287 1289 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">++</sup>
###xml 1301 1307 1283 1289 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT<sup>++</sup></italic>
###xml 1339 1341 1317 1319 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">++</sup>
###xml 1324 1341 1306 1319 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;mexEF mexT<sup>++</sup></italic>
###xml 1368 1372 1346 1350 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexE</italic>
###xml 1374 1378 1352 1356 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexF</italic>
###xml 1383 1387 1361 1365 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">oprN</italic>
###xml 1465 1473 1443 1451 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 1630 1638 1608 1616 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 2501 2510 2479 2488 <label xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 1.</label>
###xml 2511 2512 2489 2490 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</bold>
###xml 2517 2518 2495 2496 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B</bold>
###xml 2598 2599 2576 2577 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">M</italic>
###xml 2652 2653 2630 2631 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</italic>

###xml 2510 3656 2488 3626 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="34">(<bold>A</bold> and <bold>B</bold>) MA-plots showing the relationship between the logarithmic mean signal ratios, <italic>M</italic> value, and the logarithmic mean signal intensities, <italic>A</italic> value, are used to spot genes whose expression is significantly altered in (A) PAO1 <italic>mexT<sup>++</sup></italic> compared to PAO1 and (B) PAO1 <italic>mexT<sup>++</sup></italic> compared to PAO1<italic>&#916;mexEF mexT<sup>+</sup><sup>+</sup></italic>. The spots representing genes altered more than 10-fold are labelled in red. A positive <italic>M</italic> value indicates increased gene expression, while a negative value indicates reduced expression. (<bold>C</bold>) 3D scatter-plot projecting the logarithmic mean signal intensities obtained from PAO1, PAO1 <italic>mexT<sup>++</sup></italic> and PAO1<italic>&#916;mexEF mexT<sup>++</sup></italic> is used to spot genes whose expression was altered by overexpressing MexT dependent or independent of the MexEF-OprN efflux pump. (Left) The orientation of the main cloud body is adjusted towards the reader, genes highly activated by overexpressing MexT independent of the MexEF-OprN efflux pump are grouped in the red oval and genes highly reduced by overexpressing MexT dependent of the MexEF-OprN efflux pump are grouped in the green oval. (Right) The orientation of the main cloud body is adjusted to show the full scale.</p>

textid="38"><sup>c</sup>Fold change in gene expression of PAO1<italic>&#916;mexEF</italic> (pME6032-<italic>mexT</italic>) compared to PAO1 (pME6032-<italic>mexT</italic> ).</p></fn></table-wrap-foot></table-wrap>
Genespring GX software was used to analyse the data () and MA and 3D scatter plots were used to visually compare the overall gene expression profiles of all three samples (Figure 1). Overexpressing mexT in PAO1 wild-type (PAO1 mexT++) increased the expression of 36 genes and decreased the expression of 76 genes compared to PAO1 harbouring the pME6032 empty vector (>/=2-fold, P </= 0.05; see ). The most significantly altered genes (>/=10-fold) are summarized in Table 2, and include 17 genes upregulated and 23 genes downregulated by overexpressing MexT in wild-type. These genes were also indicated as the most significantly altered genes in the MA plot in Figure 1A. To test if this modulation in gene expression was dependent on the MexEF-OprN pump, the transcriptome profile of PAO1DeltamexEF mexT++ was compared with PAO1 mexT++. Eighteen of the genes downregulated by MexT in wild-type were upregulated in PAO1DeltamexEF mexT++, indicating their regulation was dependent on mexEF expression. In contrast, none of the 17 genes (apart from the mexEF-oprN operon) induced by MexT in wild-type was altered in PAO1DeltamexEF mexT++ compared to PAO1 mexT++ (Table 2), indicating their induction by MexT was independent of mexEF expression. This was also evident from the changes in MA plot of PAO1 mexT++ compared to PAO1DeltamexEF mexT++ whereby only three genes (mexE, mexF and oprN) were indicated as being highly induced, while 18 genes were highly reduced (Figure 1B). The differentiation of regulatory effects of MexT with regard to their dependency on the MexEF-OprN efflux pump was also evident in the 3D scatter plot (Figure 1C). The expression of the majority of genes was similar among the three samples, forming the main cloud body. In contrast, genes whose expression was highly altered were positioned out of the main cloud body in the 3D scatter plot. These were further categorized into two groups: one incorporating the genes induced by overexpressing MexT independent of MexEF-OprN (in red oval) and the second incorporating the genes downregulated by overexpressing MexT dependent of MexEF-OprN (in green oval). This supports the MA plot analysis and demonstrates that the most significant induction in gene expression by MexT is independent of MexEF-OprN efflux pump, while the most significant reduction by MexT is dependent of MexEF-OprN, in the condition tested. These results support our hypothesis that the genes highly induced by MexT are direct targets of the regulator. ###xml 752 759 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
To test the validity of the microarray data, genes whose expression was significantly altered (PA4881, pqsA and lldP) were selected for semi-quantitative reverse transcription PCR analysis (Figure 2). RNA was prepared from biological replicates not used in the arrays. The housekeeping gene clpX was used as the internal control. The transcript level of PA4881 was induced by overexpressing MexT in both PAO1 and PAO1DeltamexEF strains but was not detectable in the PAO1 strain containing pME6032. The transcript levels of pqsA and lldP were reduced by overexpressing MexT in PAO1 but not in PAO1DeltamexEF strains. Furthermore, the expression from promoter fusions of a selected number of genes were analysed in the wild-type PAO1 and a heterogeneous E. coli background, with and without pME6032-mexT, and all genes were highly induced by overexpressing MexT in both backgrounds (Table 3). In all cases, the results confirmed the microarray data. ###begin p 44
###xml 329 339 329 339 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexEF-oprN</italic>
###xml 384 387 384 387 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pqs</italic>
###xml 392 395 392 395 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">phn</italic>
###xml 537 541 537 541 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>
###xml 614 616 610 612 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">++</sup>
###xml 599 616 599 612 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;mexEF mexT<sup>++</sup></italic>
###xml 638 639 634 635 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 639 640 635 636 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 634 641 630 637 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT<sup>+</sup><sup>+</sup>.</italic>
###xml 657 660 653 656 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">hcn</italic>
###xml 778 783 774 779 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT,</italic>
###xml 790 794 786 790 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">hcnA</italic>
###xml 841 843 833 835 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">++</sup>
###xml 826 843 822 835 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;mexEF mexT<sup>++</sup></italic>
###xml 865 866 857 858 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 866 867 858 859 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 861 868 853 860 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT<sup>+</sup><sup>+</sup>.</italic>
###xml 924 928 916 920 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">hcnB</italic>
###xml 958 962 950 954 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>
###xml 993 1003 985 991 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;mexEF</italic>
###xml 1062 1064 1050 1052 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B18">18</xref>
###xml 1094 1097 1082 1085 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pqs</italic>
###xml 1102 1105 1090 1093 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">hcn</italic>
###xml 1273 1276 1261 1264 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pqs</italic>
###xml 1281 1284 1269 1272 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">hcn</italic>
###xml 1359 1363 1347 1351 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nfxC</italic>
###xml 1398 1408 1386 1396 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexEF-oprN</italic>
###xml 1410 1412 1398 1400 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B10">10</xref>
###xml 1472 1477 1460 1465 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lldPD</italic>
Due to the limited number and lack of good annotation of the significantly altered genes in the expression profiles (), the pathway mapping through main pathway databases such as KEGG () provided limited information. However, the expression of several operons with known cellular functions was significantly altered by MexT in a mexEF-oprN-dependent way. The transcript levels of the pqs and phn operon genes, encoding enzymes involved in the synthesis of PQS signal molecules, showed a 30- to 220-fold reduction in PAO1 wild-type, when mexT was overexpressed and a 23- to 240-fold induction in PAO1DeltamexEF mexT++ relative to PAO1 mexT++. Similarly, the hcn operon genes, encoding hydrogen cyanide synthase, showed a 11- to 52-fold reduction in PAO1 wild-type overexpressing mexT, while hcnA was upregulated 11-fold in PAO1DeltamexEF mexT++ relative to PAO1 mexT++. Previously we demonstrated a considerable reduction in hcnB expression by overexpressing mexT in PAO1 strain but not in PAO1DeltamexEF strain using semi-quantitative reverse transcription PCR (18). Our results indicated that pqs and hcn operons were indirect targets of MexT, as the modulation in expression was dependent on the overexpression of the MexEF-OprN efflux pump. A reduction in expression of pqs and hcn operons was also observed previously in the transcriptome profiling of an nfxC-type mutant strain overexpressing mexEF-oprN (10). The microarray data presented here also suggest that the lldPD operon (PA4770-PA4772), PA3326, and the PA3331-PA3334 operon are novel MexEF-OprN-dependent indirect targets of MexT.
###end p 44
###begin p 45
###xml 67 72 67 72 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexS,</italic>
###xml 123 124 123 124 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B6">6</xref>
###xml 131 135 131 135 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexS</italic>
###xml 164 168 164 168 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>
###xml 274 276 274 276 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B13">13</xref>
###xml 310 314 310 314 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexS</italic>
###xml 420 422 416 418 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">++</sup>
###xml 405 422 405 418 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;mexEF mexT<sup>++</sup></italic>
###xml 444 446 440 442 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">++</sup>
###xml 440 446 436 442 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT<sup>++</sup></italic>
###xml 448 455 444 451 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T2">Table 2</xref>
###xml 499 503 495 499 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexS</italic>
###xml 545 558 541 554 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 545 563 <span type="species:ncbi:208964">P. aeruginosa PAO1</span>
The set of genes upregulated by MexT independent of MexEF included mexS, previously shown to be activated by MexT in PAO1 (6). The mexS gene is located adjacent to mexT and divergently transcribed, which is a typical arrangement of genes controlled by LysR-type activators (13). In our transcriptome data, the mexS transcript level increased 75-fold in PAO1 overexpressing MexT and was not changed in PAO1DeltamexEF mexT++ relative to PAO1 mexT++ (Table 2). These data supported the hypothesis that mexS is an MexE-independent target of MexT in P. aeruginosa PAO1.
###end p 45
###begin p 46
###xml 59 63 59 63 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>
###xml 91 98 91 98 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T2">Table 2</xref>
Twelve additional genes were upregulated by overexpressing mexT independent of MexEF-OprN (Table 2). Most of these genes were annotated as of unknown function but included genes with probable transporter functions; PA2813-PA2811 encode components of a probable ABC transporter and the PA4354-PA4356 operon encodes a putative repressor, a probable major facilitator superfamily (MFS) transporter and a xenobiotic reductase, respectively. We hypothesized that this set of genes includes direct positively regulated targets of MexT and suggests that MexT may be a key regulator of cellular homeostasis.
###end p 46
###begin title 47
Identification of a conserved DNA motif required for MexT regulated expression.
###end title 47
###begin p 48
###xml 190 195 188 193 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexEF</italic>

###xml 1120 1124 1116 1120 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexE</italic>
###xml 1126 1127 1122 1123 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B6">6</xref>
###xml 1130 1139 1126 1135 <label xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 3.</label>

###xml 1224 1237 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
In order to identify possible direct targets of MexT and a potential consensus sequence for MexT binding, the genes that were most highly induced (>/=10-fold) by MexT in PAO1 independent of mexEF were selected for further analysis (Table 2). In addition to mexS and mexEF-oprN, the 12 genes showing induction >/=10-fold were PA1744, PA1970, PA2486, PA2759, PA2813-PA2811, PA3205, PA3229, PA4354, PA4623 and PA4881. The DNA sequence of the upstream regulatory region (-500 bp from the ATG translational start site) of each gene (including PA2813 only of the PA2813-PA2811 operon) was aligned using MEME Suite online software (24). A well-conserved DNA motif ATCA-N5-GTCGAT-N4-ACYAT was identified in the upstream regions of 9 of the 12 genes and mexE (Figure 3). Interestingly, a clear consensus sequence was not identified in the mexS promoter region. The DNA motif overlapped the ATC-N9-GAT sequence, referred to as a 'nod-box' and proposed as the general motif of the binding sites for LysR-family proteins (13). Previously, this 'nod-box' was proposed to be part of the binding site of MexT in the upstream region of mexE (6). Figure 3.Alignment of the predicted conserved DNA motif in the upstream regulatory regions of P. aeruginosa genes highly induced by MexT (A) and sequence logo for the conserved DNA motif reflecting position-specific probability matrixes (B) deduced from MEME software analysis. Nucleotides with high probability (>/=70%) are highlighted by red. The number of nucleotides between the conserved DNA motif and the start codon ATG is shown in brackets.
###end p 48
###begin p 49

###begin p 50
###xml 91 95 91 95 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lacZ</italic>
###xml 265 272 265 272 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T3">Table 3</xref>
###xml 443 447 443 447 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>
###xml 487 494 487 494 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T3">Table 3</xref>
###xml 575 579 575 579 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nfxC</italic>
###xml 594 595 594 595 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B7">7</xref>
###xml 651 655 651 655 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nfxC</italic>
###xml 694 698 694 698 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nfxC</italic>
###xml 864 868 860 864 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nfxC</italic>
###xml 883 884 879 880 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B7">7</xref>
###xml 911 915 907 911 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lacZ</italic>
###xml 960 964 956 960 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nfxC</italic>
###xml 1054 1058 1050 1054 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexE</italic>
###xml 1060 1067 1056 1063 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T3">Table 3</xref>
###xml 1079 1083 1075 1079 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>
###xml 1109 1113 1105 1109 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nfxC</italic>
###xml 1172 1179 1168 1175 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T3">Table 3</xref>
###xml 1203 1207 1199 1203 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nfxC</italic>
###xml 1417 1421 1413 1417 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nfxC</italic>
To confirm the transcriptional activation of these putative target genes by MexT, promoter-lacZ fusions of selected genes were constructed, transformed into strains of different genetic backgrounds and the level of expression monitored when MexT was overexpressed (Table 3). In the wild-type PAO1 strains, the expression level of all the promoters containing the newly deduced conserved DNA motif was highly induced by co-transforming pME6032-mexT, compared to the empty vector control (Table 3). As MexEF-OprN is normally quiescent in wild-type cells, but highly induced in nfxC-type mutants (7), we investigated if the genes were also induced in an nfxC-type mutant background. Therefore, an nfxC-type mutant was generated by plating the wild-type strain PAO1 on LB agar plates containing chloramphenicol at 600 microg/ml, a condition previously shown to select nfxC-type mutants (7). A selection of promoter-lacZ fusion constructs were transformed into the nfxC mutant and high levels of expression were observed from all constructs tested, including mexE (Table 3). When the mexT gene was deleted in this nfxC-type mutant the expression of these genes was attenuated (Table 3). We also tested other nfxC-type mutant strains from different sources, and all of them showed high induction of PA4881 (data not shown). These results indicated that all the genes with the conserved DNA motif were highly induced in the nfxC-type mutant strains and thus, induced by MexT in physiologically relevant conditions.
###end p 50
###begin p 51
###xml 136 143 136 143 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 169 173 169 173 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lacZ</italic>
###xml 202 206 202 206 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>
###xml 247 254 247 254 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 277 281 273 277 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>
###xml 305 309 301 305 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>

###xml 377 384 373 380 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T2">Table 2</xref>

###xml 905 912 901 908 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T3">Table 3</xref>
###xml 1025 1038 1021 1034 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 1109 1113 1105 1109 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>

###xml 1512 1514 1504 1506 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B25">25</xref>
###xml 1761 1765 1753 1757 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>
###xml 1791 1792 1783 1784 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B9">9</xref>
###xml 1933 1937 1925 1929 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mexT</italic>
###xml 2315 2319 2307 2311 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nfxC</italic>
###xml 2341 2348 2333 2340 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 2359 2366 2347 2354 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T3">Table 3</xref>
###xml 136 143 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 247 254 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 334 352 <span type="species:ncbi:208964">P. aeruginosa PAO1</span>
###xml 399 406 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 628 635 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 754 761 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1025 1038 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 1423 1430 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 2341 2348 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
To further investigate if these genes are direct targets of MexT, we assessed if MexT could activate their expression in a heterogenous E. coli background. The promoter-lacZ fusion plasmids and pME6032-mexT or pME6032 were co-transformed into the E. coli DH5alpha strains. The mexT gene cloned in pME6032-mexT was highly expressed in P. aeruginosa PAO1 without IPTG induction (Table 2). However, in E. coli, the native mexT promoter was not induced and IPTG induction was essential for full activation (data not shown). Therefore, a saturated concentration of IPTG (1 mM) was used to induce mexT expression from pME6032-mexT in E. coli. As shown in Table 3, low expression levels of the putative MexT target promoters, including mexE was observed in the E. coli strains containing empty vector pME6032. In contrast, when mexT was overexpressed, the expression of the promoters were significantly induced (Table 3). These results indicate that MexT may directly activate the expression of the newly identified target genes in P. aeruginosa. This was further supported by the observation that an overexpressing mexT construct, cloned from a different PAO1 wild-type available in the laboratory collection, and which contained a single base-pair mutation that resulted in an alanine to valine (A to V) change in the 39th residue of the MexT protein, failed to induce the expression of these promoter fusions in either PAO1 or E. coli DH5alpha backgrounds (data not shown). According to the Pfam database alignment (25), the 39th residue is located in the helix-turn-helix motif of MexT, the DNA-binding motif of the protein. Indeed our results suggested that a mutation in this domain rendered the protein non-functional. While other inactivating mutations in the mexT gene have been reported (9) this single base pair mutation has not been previously identified in wild-type strains and appears to be a novel mechanism of inactivating mexT. Subsequently, to confirm that the conserved DNA motif in the promoter region was required for MexT activation of the putative target genes, site-directed mutagenesis was carried out to mutate GTCGAT to GTCTGT in the DNA motif of PA4623 and PA4881 promoters. This alteration in the DNA motif completely attenuated activation of the promoters by MexT in the wild-type PAO1, PAO1nfxC and the heterogenous E. coli DH5alpha (Table 3). Thus, the conserved DNA motif is required for the induced expression of these genes by MexT.
###end p 51
###begin title 52
MexT protein binds to the conserved DNA motif in target promoters
###end title 52
###begin p 53
###xml 221 225 221 225 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lacZ</italic>

###xml 236 243 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
In order to verify if the MexT protein directly binds the conserved DNA motif, a plasmid expressing C-terminal His-tagged MexT protein was constructed. This tagged MexT protein activated the expression of PA4881 promoter-lacZ fusion in E. coli, indicating the protein was functional (data now shown). EMSAs were performed to detect binding of MexT to two 207-bp DNA fragments containing the unaltered or mutated PA4881 promoter region. The MexT protein clearly bound to the DNA fragments containing the intact conserved DNA motif (Figure 4A), but not to the DNA fragments containing the mutated conserved DNA motif (Figure 4B). The specificity of MexT binding to its DNA target was confirmed by a competition assay with an excess of unlabeled target DNA (). These results demonstrated, for the first time, that MexT protein bound to the conserved DNA motif and that a mutation in two of the most conserved nucleotides in the motif abolished the binding of the MexT protein. Figure 4.Purified MexT protein binds to the conserved DNA motif in the promoter region of PA4881. EMSAs were carried out applying 0 ng, 37.5 ng, 75 ng, 150 ng and 300 ng (lanes O, 1, 2, 3 and 4) of purified His6-tagged functional (A and B) or non functional (C) MexT proteins to 10 fmol of DIG-labelled DNA target containing the intact conserved DNA motif (A and C), or the mutated DNA target with the conserved DNA motif disrupted (B). Arrow indicates the free DNA probes and the band shifts of the MexT-DNA complex.

###begin p 55
###xml 332 340 332 340 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F4">Figure 4</xref>
To further investigate MexT binding to this conserved motif, the residue 39 A to V mutated non-functional MexT was purified using the His-tag expression plasmid previously used for the wild-type MexT protein. EMSAs were performed to detect binding of the mutated MexT protein to the conserved DNA motif and no binding was detected (Figure 4C). These results demonstrated that this particular mutation in the helix-turn-helix motif abolished the binding of MexT protein to the target DNA.

MexT activates the expression of target genes across other Pseudomonas species
